Optimized Prompts for Agent Communication & Continuity
1. Agent Handoff/Continuity Document Update
Prompt:
*"Update the continuity document to reflect the current status of the app build. Include:

Current Phase: [e.g., 'Architecture Design']
Completed Tasks: [e.g., 'Module A validated']
Pending Tasks: [e.g., 'Module B testing']
Priorities: [e.g., 'Testing > New Features']
Philosophy: 'Slow is smooth, smooth is fast. Avoid scope creep.'
Next Steps: [e.g., 'Build Module B']
Exclude confidence scores or unnecessary details. Keep it actionable."*

User Expectation:
The next agent will immediately understand the project’s status, priorities, and next steps without sifting through irrelevant information.

2. Plan Review & Validation
Prompt:
*"Review the current plan for:

Logical Flow: Does each phase build on the previous one?
Risk Mitigation: Are there checkpoints for testing/validation?
Agent Clarity: Can a new agent pick up seamlessly after a crash?
Scope Creep: Are all tasks directly tied to the core app?
Flag any issues or ambiguities. Update the plan only if necessary."*

User Expectation:
The plan is vetted for safety, clarity, and alignment with your goals before execution begins.

3. Module-Level Execution
Prompt:
*"For the current module:

Define: Purpose, inputs, outputs, and dependencies.
Build: Proceed only if the design is validated.
Test: Confirm functionality and edge cases.
Document: Update continuity docs for this module.
Stop immediately if any step fails or risks disrupting the build."*

User Expectation:
Each module is built, tested, and documented independently, minimizing risk to the overall project.

4. Debugging & Validation Checkpoint
Prompt:
*"At each checkpoint:

Debug: Identify and resolve issues in the current module.
Validate: Confirm alignment with the overall architecture.
Communicate: Update continuity docs with findings.
If a fix risks progress, flag it for review before acting."*

User Expectation:
Issues are caught early, and the project remains on track without unnecessary disruptions.

5. Discretionary Improvements
Prompt:
*"If you identify a potential improvement:

Assess ROI: Will it significantly enhance functionality without risk?
Check Scope: Does it align with the core app or introduce creep?
Propose: Only if it passes both checks, suggest it for review.
Never implement without explicit approval."*

User Expectation:
Improvements are considered but never at the cost of stability or scope.

Current Status

Plan: Reviewed and optimized for incremental, low-risk progress.
Next Step: Validate the architecture design (Phase 1) with you before proceeding.
Continuity Docs: Ready for updates after each phase.

Phase 1: Architecture Design & Validation
Objective
Define the high-level architecture of the application, including core modules, their interactions, and dependencies. Validate the design using mockups or flowcharts to ensure clarity and feasibility before moving to implementation.

Steps


Define Core Modules:

Identify the key functional components of the application (e.g., user interface, data processing, API integrations, database).
Document the purpose, inputs, outputs, and dependencies for each module.



Map Module Interactions:

Create a flowchart or diagram to visualize how modules interact.
Ensure data flows logically between modules and aligns with the application's objectives.



Validate with Mockups:

Develop wireframes or mockups for the user interface (if applicable) to visualize the user experience.
Use tools like Lucidchart, Draw.io, or even simple sketches to represent the architecture.



Review with Stakeholders (You):

Present the architecture design and mockups for feedback.
Confirm alignment with your vision and business objectives.



Document the Architecture:

Update the continuity document with the validated architecture, including:

Module descriptions.
Interaction diagrams.
Mockups or flowcharts.
Any assumptions or constraints.
